Sports News

National Sports Association Announces Regulations for Far Eastern Games Preliminary Selection 151

▲Track and field all-around basketball to be held in Shanghai in mid-April

▲Football and men's swimming to be held in Hong Kong in April

The general methods for selecting various sports for participation in the 10th Far Eastern Games have been decided and announced by the board of directors of the National Sports Advancement Association (reported on the 12th). Now, the association officially announces the detailed competition regulations for each item as follows:

Track and Field and All-Around

㈠ Date of preliminary selection: April 14th and 15th,

㈡ Location: Shanghai,

㈢ Those who wish to participate in the competition must have passing standard scores (listed in the newspapers on the 13th). Application should be submitted by sports organizations of provinces, cities, special districts, or overseas Chinese groups.

㈣ Application period: Starts today and ends on April 10th (based on the date the list is received).

㈤ Application address: Shanghai China National Sports Advancement Association,

㈥ Application fee: One yuan per person per sport,

㈦ After the preliminary selection, the selection committee hired by the association will select official representatives for each sport to participate in the Far Eastern Games. The selection method will be based on performance, without setting a fixed number of people.

㈧ Travel and food expenses for athletes from various regions participating in the preliminary selection will be borne by themselves.

㈨ The association will be responsible for the round-trip travel expenses of the selected athletes to Shanghai.

㈩ After the official team members are selected, they will stay in Shanghai for training, and the association will provide food and accommodation.

Basketball

㈠ Date: Starting from April 14th,

㈡ Location: Shanghai China Basketball Hall,

㈢ The preliminary selection will take the North China team as the basic team. Those other teams who wish to participate in the competition should apply in the name of provinces, cities, special districts, or overseas Chinese groups, and application should be submitted by the sports organizations of each unit.

㈣ Application period: Starts today and ends on April 10th (based on the date the list is received).

㈤ Application address: Shanghai China National Sports Advancement Association,

㈥ The travel expenses to and from Shanghai and the stay in Shanghai for each team participating in the competition shall be borne by themselves.

㈦ Preliminary selection competition method: If two or more teams apply besides the North China team, a knockout system will be used for the competition. The winning team will then compete with the North China team in the finals.

㈧ After the preliminary selection, the selection committee hired by the association will select twelve people with excellent skills to serve as representatives to participate in the Far Eastern Games (not based on the team).

㈨ The officially selected team will stay in Shanghai for training with food and accommodation provided by the association. 　㈩ The association will be responsible for the round-trip travel expenses of the selected players to Shanghai.

Football

㈠ Location: Hong Kong,

㈡ Date: Around April 20th,

㈢ Application period: Starts today and ends on April 15th.

㈣ Application address: South China Athletic Association, 8th Floor, China Building, Hong Kong Avenue, forwarded to the Hong Kong Chinese Sports Advancement Association,

㈤ Teams wishing to participate in the competition should apply in the name of provinces, cities, special districts, or overseas Chinese groups, and application should be submitted by the sports organizations of each unit.

㈥ The preliminary selection competition method is to be determined.

㈦ After the preliminary selection, the selection committee hired by the association will select seventeen people with excellent skills to serve as representatives to participate in the Far Eastern Games (not based on the team).

(Note) No preliminary selection will be held for men's and women's volleyball teams.

Swimming

㈠ Date: Starting from April 18th,

㈡ Location: Held simultaneously in Hong Kong and Shanghai,

㈢ Those who wish to participate in the competition must have passing standard scores (listed in the newspapers on the 13th). Application should be submitted by the sports organizations of the relevant provinces, cities, special districts, or overseas Chinese groups.

㈣ Application period: Starts today and ends on April 10th (based on the date the application is received).

㈤ Application address: ㈠ Shanghai China National Sports Advancement Association, ㈡ South China Athletic Association, 8th Floor, China Building, Hong Kong Avenue, forwarded to the Hong Kong Chinese Sports Advancement Association,

㈥ Application fee: One yuan per person per sport,

㈦ Travel expenses to Shanghai or Hong Kong for athletes from various regions participating in the competition shall be borne by themselves.

㈧ After the preliminary selection, the selection committee hired by the association will select official representatives for each sport based on performance to participate in the Far Eastern Games (number of people is not fixed).

㈨ The association will be responsible for the round-trip travel expenses of the selected athletes to Shanghai or Hong Kong.

㈩ After the official team members are selected, the association will provide them with food and accommodation and they will stay in Hong Kong or Shanghai for training.

Introduction to the History and Achievements of the Far Eastern Games 157

▲Edited by Ruan Weicun▲Checked by Shen Siliang

The 10th Far Eastern Games will be held in the Philippines on May 12th. There are only a little over a month left until the meeting. Both Japan and the Philippines are actively preparing. It has been twenty years since the Far Eastern Games began, and our country has sent people to participate in every event and hosted the second, fifth, and eighth games. However, few people pay attention to the history and achievements of past games, and there are no special books to record them. Recently, the "History and Achievements of the Far Eastern Games" published by Qinfen Bookstore at 392 Labor Father Road, French Concession, Shanghai (across from the National Sports Advancement Association) was edited by Ruan Weicun and proofread by Shen Siliang, the main member of the China National Sports Advancement Association. The various records and photos in the book took ten years to collect. It details the proceedings of past games and the official records of track and field, all-around, swimming, football, basketball, volleyball, tennis, baseball, cycling, women's tennis, and women's volleyball. It also includes detailed information on the list of athletes in past games, the schedule and venues of past games, the presidents of past games, and the championship results of past games. The most valuable thing in the book is the hundreds of photos, such as photos of the founder of the games, photos of the trophies donated by Yuan Shikai and Li Yuanhong, photos of the winning teams in each event from the first to the ninth games, and photos of individual winners, which are dazzling and spectacular. The entire book is a thick volume and sells for only 9 jiao and 5 fen, plus 1 jiao and 1 fen for registered postage for out-of-town mail orders. The store's storefront is located at 554 Fourth Malu, British Concession, Shanghai.

The Development of Domestic Sports Goods by Dahua Company 158

Because Chinese people feel that most sports goods depend on imports, they are striving to manufacture their own products. Dahua Sports Equipment Company is the strongest pioneer in being able to compete with imported goods in the market at the lowest prices. Dahua products have gained a considerable position and reputation in society and are striving to improve their work. Therefore, the products are becoming more and more refined and the position is becoming more and more consolidated. In addition to establishing branches in various cities such as Suzhou and Changzhou, they also plan to expand to North China so that customers in various places can have the opportunity to purchase nearby. The company has recently held a clearance sale and is giving away domestic daily necessities, welcoming groups to visit and provide guidance.

Since its opening, the Ziqiang Sports Goods Store in Taipingqiao, French Concession, Shanghai, has been well received by the sports community for its excellent products and low prices. The Sports Department of Nanjing Central University ordered a batch of German handballs from the store, which has now been manufactured. The raw materials are domestic products, and the style is exactly the same as German handballs. The first batch was shipped to Nanjing last week. Now the Sports Department of Central University has decided to add another batch, which is currently being rushed to make and will be shipped soon. If large, medium, and small schools in various cities need this German handball, they can order from the store for delivery on a specific date.

Zhejiang Education Department Organizes Film Patrol Team 161

▲Ten Measures Defined... Patrol Routes Focus on Rural Areas

—No Admission Fee—

Film performances are the most realistic and touching. Educational films are promoted by European and American countries, especially with great effort. If this type of film can be popularized throughout the country and penetrate into rural areas, its effectiveness will be great. The capital and Shanghai in our country have achieved great results in implementing educational films, and all provinces are planning to promote them. Zhejiang Province also needs it urgently. It is said that the Education Department, in view of this, plans to first organize a film patrol team to tour various counties to screen educational films, starting in May this year. The required start-up costs will be transferred from the provincial education funds for this year. The "Measures for Screening Educational Films by the Zhejiang Provincial Education Department Film Patrol Team" and the "Budget for Start-up Costs and Recurring Expenses" were drafted and submitted to the Provincial Government Committee for deliberation. 　　、　　　Screening measures, ㈠ In order to enlighten the people, revitalize rural areas, assist school education, and promote social education, the Zhejiang Provincial Department of Education organizes a film patrol team to screen educational films. ㈡ The film patrol team consists of one officer, one mechanic, and accompanying film machinery and all equipment to tour the counties for screening. ㈢ When the film patrol team arrives in each county, the county government should, in accordance with the following principles, jointly plan the patrol route, screening venues, and screening times, etc.: 1. The patrol route focuses on rural areas; 2. The screening venues borrow public places such as schools, temples, and ancestral halls; 3. The screening time can be day or night; 4. A maximum of four screenings per day; 5. The tour date for each county is based on one or two weeks; ㈣ After the route, venue, and time are determined, the county government shall notify the autonomous organizations, public security organizations, and educational organizations in the areas passed through to assist in the implementation and fill out a preliminary tour screening report to be submitted to the Education Department for verification; ㈤ All expenses required by the film patrol team shall be paid by the Provincial Education Department under the expense item and shall not be supplied by the local government. However, officers and mechanics may borrow educational institutions or public venues to live in; ㈥ Screening educational films will absolutely not collect admission fees from the audience. However, the number of visitors may be moderately limited to avoid crowding; ㈦ During the screening, the officer should explain the situation in the film in detail to ensure that the audience fully understands; ㈧ In addition to screening educational films, the film patrol team should also prepare auxiliary tools for lectures and conduct popular lectures before and after the screening; ㈨ After the tour and screening in each county is completed, the officer should fill out a tour screening work report and submit it to the Education Department for verification; ㈩ These measures shall be implemented from the date of promulgation by the Zhejiang Provincial Education Department.

Handover of Film Examination Committee 162

The Film Examination Committee jointly formed by the Ministry of Interior and the Ministry of Education is now being changed to be affiliated to the Party Department instead of the administrative organ. The Central Film Enterprise Guidance Committee of the Central Propaganda Committee has hired Luo Gang, Dai Ce, and other seven people to be responsible for examining films. (The association is still named the Film Examination Committee and is affiliated with the Film Enterprise Guidance Committee.) The reorganized meeting has been established. The Central Film Enterprise Guidance Committee dispatched Luo Gang, the director of the examination committee, to the Film Examination Committee jointly formed by the Ministry of Interior and the Ministry of Education to receive the examination committee from 3:00 PM to 4:00 PM yesterday (20th). During the receiving procedures, the responsible committee members of the association jointly formed by the Ministry of Interior and the Ministry of Education (Li Jingbi, the internal editor, and Li Jiaxiang, the commissioner of the Ministry of Education) returned the film equipment and documents to the association. Yang Junli, the second section chief of the Police Department of the Ministry of Interior, and Zhang Jiong, the director of the Social Department of the Ministry of Education, counted them before handing them over to Luo Gang, the director of the reorganization. It is said that the reorganized examination committee's office will be located in Er Tiao Xiang, and it is currently temporarily borrowing the original place in the Education Department auditorium to examine films for a period of three weeks. After the office in Er Tiao Xiang is deployed, it will be moved in. The receiving on the 20th was for machines and documents. The old association jointly formed by the Ministry of Interior and the Ministry of Education will handle the accounting for two months in order to report to the Audit Department. As for the old association's organization, in addition to the seven committee members sent by the Ministry of Interior and the Ministry of Education, who each receive their original salary in the department and receive a transportation allowance of 30 yuan in the association, there are also four staff members (monthly salary of 180 yuan, 160 yuan, 120 yuan, and 100 yuan respectively), and nine clerks (the chief clerk receives 80 yuan, and the rest receive 40 to 50 yuan). The monthly expenditure was about 1,000 yuan. The new association's director receives 200 yuan, and the remaining six people receive 100 to 100 yuan respectively. Moreover, according to the regulations, 4 to 6 staff members and a number of clerks can be set up, and the expenses are all paid by the association. The scope is slightly larger than the old association, and the Central Propaganda Committee will request the central government to subsidize the original expenses. It is also said that more than a dozen staff members and clerks of the old association will be reorganized by the new association.

(三) Open all municipal parks and private gardens to children for free access (request Committee Member Qiu Xisheng to handle this matter). (四) Open all administrative and military organs and major factories in the city for children to visit for one week starting from Children's Day (request Committee Member Cai Hongtian to handle this matter). (五) Request aviation authorities to dispatch more aircraft to fly over the city to celebrate Children's Day and distribute slogans to make children pay attention to aviation (to be handled by Committee Member Hu Shuyi). (六) Hold a children's health competition on Children's Day (request Sun Jiaqi to draft the measures and submit them for decision at the next meeting). (七) Notify citizens that families should pay more attention to children's cleanliness on Children's Day and create an environment suitable for children's lives to foster a concept of valuing Children's Day (to be handled by the Children's Happiness Committee). (八) Issue special editions of Children's Day in various newspapers (to be handled by the Children's Happiness Committee). (九) Request all banks to give children high-interest savings for one week starting from Children's Day to develop children's savings habits (request Committee Member Qiu Xisheng to handle this matter). ㈣ How to find ways to entertain children throughout the city. It was resolved to request Committee Member Qiu Xisheng to draft a plan and submit it to the next meeting for a decision. ㈤ Preparing for an exhibition of children's books and children's toys for Children's Day. It was resolved to request the Education Bureau to instruct the Shanghai Municipal People's Education Center to handle it. ㈥ Holding a model children's competition. It was resolved to request the Children's Happiness Committee to draft measures and send a letter to the Education Bureau to handle it. ㈦ Suggesting that the municipal government establish a new undertaking beneficial to children every Children's Day. The resolution was passed and the Children's Happiness Committee was requested to handle it. ㈧ Preparing the funds for celebrating this year's Children's Day. Municipal Education Bureau Issues Orders to Promulgate Revised Measures for Dental Clinics 166

▲ And the Schedule of Clinic Dates for Each School

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau instructed all municipal primary and secondary schools, stating that according to the official letter from the Municipal Health Bureau, "Upon investigation, the number of students with dental defects in the city's schools is nearly 50% or more. Therefore, efforts must be made to improve the correction aspect. Since the establishment of the dental clinic, many schools have sent students to the clinic for treatment, but there are also many who have been slow to send them, which is not conducive to preserving children's health. Therefore, starting from this semester, new treatment measures will be implemented to improve this situation." The bureau jointly issued the treatment measures and the first set of dental clinic schedules for each school, instructing the schools to comply. The measures and schedule are transcribed as follows: (甲) Measures: ㈠ The bureau has established a complete dental clinic in the Xilin Road Health Office in the South Shanghai District, with treatment hours from 8:30 AM to 11:30 AM and 1:00 PM to 4:30 PM daily. The clinic is closed on Saturday afternoons and Sundays. ㈡ Due to limited funding, the bureau has temporarily hired one dentist and one dental assistant. To ensure detailed work, the number of people is limited to a maximum of six in the morning and no more than seven in the afternoon. ㈢ For the convenience of work, the bureau has adopted a rotating treatment system, with five schools as a group, and the time ranges from four months to ten months (treatment for new students in the second semester of the 22nd year is temporarily postponed). When the treatment of each group of five schools is completed, then the other five schools will begin. ㈣ Students with dental diseases who can independently seek treatment from other licensed dentists are free to do so. However, they must submit a certificate of recovery from the dentist to the school, and the school will then submit it to the Education Bureau for cancellation of the student's defect record. ㈤ Students with acute dental diseases, even if they are not listed in the five schools, can bring their treatment records and films to the clinic during office hours for treatment. ㈥ In addition to the five designated schools, to facilitate other schools, it is specifically stipulated that Friday afternoons and Saturday mornings are the dates for treating the dental diseases of students and teachers from other schools. However, prior consultation and scheduling with the bureau's dentists is required. If arrangements have not been made, no treatment will be provided except for emergency cases. The daily number of dental treatments will be determined by the doctor based on the preparation of the condition. ㈦ All

schools that have been examined by the bureau's health personnel have their students' dental conditions recorded in the "Defect Correction Record." This record is kept by the school, and the schools should check it frequently. From now on, schools should send six to seven students with dental diseases on time according to the scheduled dates. Those who need follow-up visits will be notified by the bureau's dental clinic at any time according to the schedule. ㈧ For each group of five designated schools, there are two schools that are farther away from the dental clinic. The Health Bureau will send a car to pick them up and drop them off, still limited to six to seven people each time. The schools should pre-arrange the students who need treatment to save time. ㈨ The equipment of dental instruments and the hiring of medical personnel consume a significant amount of municipal funds. The original purpose was to specialize in correcting students' dental diseases. If the school authorities are not attentive, it will not only waste funds but also greatly affect the health of students. From now on, if it is found that schools within the five designated schools fail to send students according to the scheduled dates, the principal of the school will be given a major demerit by the Education Bureau. After three major demerits, the principal will be dismissed. (乙) Clinic Schedule: Monday, morning: He'an; afternoon: Wuben. Tuesday, morning: Wanzhu; afternoon: Bide. Wednesday, morning: Meixi; afternoon: Wuben. Thursday, morning: He'an; afternoon: Bide. Friday, morning: Wanzhu; afternoon: other schools. Saturday, morning: Meixi and other schools.

The Science Society of China Reviews Various Academic Cases 167

▲ Terminology of Standard Weights and Measures and Sectioning of Arithmetic Naming

The Science Society of China in this city previously received a letter from the Bureau of Weights and Measures of the Ministry of Industry, seeking revisions to the draft of standard weights and measures and terminology. The Ministry of Education and the National Compilation and Translation Bureau also sought opinions on the sectioning of arithmetic naming. Recently, they also inquired about the society's opinion on the entire draft of mathematical terms. However, the society believed that these cases required the opinions of experts and a majority of people before they could be answered. Therefore, the 112th meeting of the board of directors decided that the sectioning of arithmetic naming would be discussed by the general secretary convening members of the society's astronomy and mathematics departments. The draft of mathematical terms would be reviewed by the original drafters and Mr. Gu Yangwu.

Teachers and Students of Nanyang Model Middle School Discuss Commemorating Lu Huigang 171

Lu Huigang of Nanyang Model Primary and Secondary School has been involved in education for more than 30 years, spreading his influence and knowledge widely. He was meticulous in his work, both large and small, from beginning to end, which is especially commendable. His sudden death has caused the entire school to lose its respect and admiration, and they are deeply saddened. It is reported that the teachers and students of the school, in order to commemorate Mr. Lu, have scheduled a memorial meeting at the school at 2:00 PM on the 25th of this month. The letter sent to all circles is recorded as follows: Dear Sirs/Madams, Mr. Lu Huigang has served our school for more than 30 years. He was kind and patient in his management and careful in handling affairs, both large and small. For 30 years, he devoted his life to education and greatly benefited our school. His sudden death on the ninth of January this year has caused great sorrow to the entire school. Therefore, it has been decided to hold a memorial meeting in the school auditorium at 2:00 PM on the afternoon of March 25th. All those who knew Mr. Lu are welcome to attend and pay their respects. If you have any eulogies, elegiac couplets, or epitaphs to contribute, please send them to Nanyang Model Middle School, Xujiahui, Shanghai, before March 24th so that they can be displayed and arranged. We are deeply grateful. Sincerely, All Teachers and Students of Private Nanyang Model Middle School.

Publication of the Innovative Foreign Language Learning Method 175

▲ A Guide for Middle School Students Learning Foreign Languages

The Ministry of Education announced the statistics of the graduation examination results of primary and secondary schools in various provinces and cities. Mathematics was the worst subject in both senior and junior high schools, followed by foreign languages. It was considered that special attention should be paid to urging and improving teaching methods. In fact, the time and effort spent by middle school students in studying foreign languages ​​is far more than learning other subjects, but the results of the graduation examination are still a failure. It is not that the students are unwilling to work hard, but that they have not obtained the proper learning methods. What is the loss of each middle school student after three or six years of hard work and the results are so poor? Lu Dianyuan, professor of English Teaching Methods in the Foreign Language Department of National Zhejiang University, has seen that students work hard but do not achieve results in learning foreign languages. In his spare time from teaching, he compiled and translated the book "Innovative Foreign Language Learning Method" based on scientific principles and teaching experience, introducing practical and feasible methods. If implemented according to this, it will achieve twice the result with half the effort. The book was recently published by World Book Company and the price is very low, only 25 cents per copy, in order to popularize it. At a time when various provinces and cities are holding graduation examinations and middle school students are panicking and forgetting to eat and sleep to prepare for foreign languages, which students generally recognize as difficult to learn, the publication of this book can serve as a compass for learning English and a guide for most young people. Time and effort can be used efficiently. It is advisable for middle school students to have a copy for themselves, and other self-learners of English can also purchase it for reference. President Guo of Zhejiang University wrote in the preface to his book: "If students across the country can choose the fastest way to complete their tools, so that they can browse a wide range of books and have unimpeded access, and then explore the mysteries of world academia, then Mr. Lu's book is not in vain." This is not a false statement.

Recent News from the Third Zhonghua Vocational School 176

The Third Zhonghua Vocational Supplementary School, run by the Chinese Vocational Education Society near Lujiabang Road, Xiaoximen, offers courses in machinery, electrical engineering, radio, civil engineering, architecture, drafting, English, etc., and classes are held every evening, which is very convenient for those who want to continue their studies after work. The teachers hired are all knowledgeable and experienced. The teachers of machinery and electrical engineering are all engineers from Huashang Electric Company. The teachers of radio are engineers and technicians from Dahua Radio Company and International Radio Station. As for the equipment, the electrical testing room, the mechanical workshop, and the civil engineering laboratory are all well-equipped.

Financial Market Gold Price Drops Two Yuan The U.S. House Passes the Dies Silver Bill 177

▼The Content of the Silver Bill Is Peaceful, Market Conditions Are Still Stable▲

The gold market fell yesterday due to the passage of the Dies Silver Bill in the U.S. House, effectively halting its upward momentum. However, the content of the Dies Silver Bill was moderate, resulting in relatively stable market conditions throughout the day. There was considerable buying interest when prices dipped. In the early morning, overseas silver markets in both Britain and the U.S. fell in unison. The forward silver price on the Five Metals Exchange dropped by six to eight and a half tenths of a cent. Exchange rates, on the other hand, rose. The price of raw gold in London remained unchanged. American cotton fell fifteen pounds, and American wheat fell twenty-five. The wool market opened strongly, rising to sixty-five yuan at one point. It then suddenly declined to fifty-six yuan due to a radio broadcast mentioning the passage of the American Dies Silver Bill. However, as official telegraphic news had not yet been released, buyers took advantage of the low prices, causing a rebound. Nevertheless, Reuters reported that the U.S. House had passed the Poage Bill and that the Dies Silver Bill had also passed with 257 votes against 112, making it difficult for the market to remain firm and creating a sense of fatigue. After the opening, the exchange rate market tended to ease, and news from the Associated Press and other agencies indicated that the Dies Silver Bill stipulated that foreign countries using silver to purchase American agricultural products should be charged 25% above the world market price, leading to a further decline. However, Reuters also reported that U.S. House Speaker Rayburn announced the Frear Silver Bill, which proposed that the government purchase 1.5 billion ounces of silver until prices returned to the 1926 level, and that discussions were suspended at the President's request, resulting in some recovery. Despite this, the exchange rate market hardened, and individual investors aggressively sold, pushing prices down. Reuters' U.S. market report stated that the silver bill's passage after the market closed led to expectations of a fifty-pound increase in the opening price the following morning, as well as increased capital for rural lending banks to relieve rural areas. Prices fell again at noon but remained stable at the close. The overall market outlook was stable, and sentiment tended towards peace. There was a lot of short covering, and prices remained high. Although there were rumors of rising silver prices in the overnight market, they had little impact. The day's market conditions are recorded as follows:

Increased Complexity of Bank Clearing 179

The market situation of the silver and money industry can be traced back to mid-January at the beginning of the year. Due to the slack season for various industries, there was an urgent need for clearing, so the market atmosphere was exceptionally desolate, with no possibility of activity. Up until the past few days, the market remained sluggish due to the poor commercial situation and cautious lending by money houses, resulting in a lack of activity. The market, which had been trying to become active, turned silent again. Starting from the day before yesterday, the market saw a slight increase in activity due to large movements of goods by foreign merchants, which led to a slightly more active flow of funds. As a result, the market became more vibrant, and clearing became more complex. The atmosphere in the market was also invigorated. However, the interbank lending rate remained unchanged due to an appropriate balance of supply and demand, with the morning and noon rates remaining at two cents. Overdrafts were also at two to three cents, and transactions in interbank bills increased. Morning turnover was over 4.7 million, with new transactions exceeding 200,000. Noon turnover was over 800,000, and transactions among small associations were over 400,000. Inflows from customer routes amounted to 100,000, and outflows amounted to 400,000. Foreign mortgage transactions amounted to 1.67 million, and banknote collection and issuance amounted to over 3.1 million. Bank clearing included foreign banks clearing over 2.67 million in various bills, over 5 million in various goods, exchange, mortgage, electricity, and miscellaneous items, and over 800,000 in foreign exchange and debt prices. Warehousing amounted to 400,000. Chinese banks cleared 3.23 million in bills, 6.45 million in various goods, exchange, tax, mortgage, and miscellaneous items, and 300,000 in warehousing. Japanese banks cleared over 2.6 million in bills, over 4.22 million in various miscellaneous items, and 600,000 in warehousing. Money houses cleared over 41.1 million in foreign public bills, over 8.2 million in foreign overdrafts, and over 800,000 in various exchange bills. Clearing involved cash reconciliation, and there were slight inflows and outflows of large bars of silver. The total number of exchanges at the local clearing house was 7,551,065.01 yuan in silver, including 3,413,998.32 yuan in silver dollars and 4,137,066.69 yuan in exchange silver dollars.

Securities High Point Triggers the Emergence of Bulls The Rising Trend of Government Bonds Seems to Have Slowed Slightly 181

The Process Remains Extremely Stable, Resulting in More Gains Than Losses

Yesterday, the Chinese Securities Exchange saw high morale, which remained unabated. However, with the rising trend lasting for too long, it triggered the emergence of bulls. There was a slight reversal at one point yesterday, but it failed to push back against the market's firm morale. The shorts also did not dare to hesitate, resulting in a missed opportunity. Therefore, as soon as there was a slight easing, someone seized the opportunity to cover, making it difficult for prices to fall in the days leading up to settlement. When the market opened yesterday morning, No. 53, with its rapid advance and planned reduction this month, was lifted by half a yuan, making the shorts feel increasingly fearful and eager to cover. Numbers 16 and 17 were also bought in, and individual investors were also shorting swaps, creating a squeeze on shorts and intensifying the situation. This led to new high price records for various bonds from 1918 onward, except for the Consolidated Tax bonds, which weakened due to aggressive selling by numbers 11 and 59. New York Stocks and Bonds Fall Across the Board 182

The Wall Street Journal's market report on the 19th stated that stocks, bonds, and commodities all fell due to labor disputes in the automotive and railway industries. Mining stocks collapsed due to the possibility that silver legislation would be delayed until the government investigated the situation in China. Market conditions on the small exchange were also weak, with special stocks being sold off continuously. German bonds fell sharply for unknown reasons, affecting the bond market. In addition, a report from the bank's New York agent stated that (securities) fell due to labor disputes and the delay in the silver bill's vote. (Wheat) fell due to the weakness of the stock market and the slight unloading by bulls. Spot prices were gradually tightening, indicating a decrease in supply. Do not sell short. (Cotton) fell sharply in the early morning. The passage of the Poage Bill led to the recovery of half the losses. There were few followers during the rise. The market was shaken by labor disputes and the growing opposition to the Recovery Bureau's proposals to reduce working hours and increase wages. Before the situation is determined, there will continue to be selling at high prices. The spot market is quiet. The Dow Jones New York Index is listed below:

Rumors of Large Amounts of Spot Yarn Delivery Selling Sentiment Spreads in the Cotton Yarn Market 183

│Golden Rooster Yarn Enters the 80 Yuan Level Consistently│

The yarn market is weakening, and the falling trend is intensifying. As the delivery deadline approaches, there are rumors in the market that a large amount of spot yarn will be delivered. It is also said that foreign merchants have a significant short position and are preparing to ship Tianjin Chinese yarn to Shanghai for delivery. At the same time, actual demand remains sluggish. Under these circumstances, sellers are reactivating, selling sentiment is rising, and the market is falling. However, the cotton market is rising again, making it more difficult for factories. However, the outlet for spot yarn is too narrow, and the pressure is relatively heavy.

Cotton Yarn Price Drops Sharply by Approximately Two Yuan The morning market opening price of cotton yarn was affected by the weak American cotton market. The buying interest in the market was lacking, and prices for each month fell by 0.09 to 0.12 yuan. There were many rumors in the afternoon, with many saying that a certain factory had another large batch of hedging sales, and the situation became more volatile. Prices for each month fell by 0.07, 0.08, 0.1 to 0.126 yuan. The total transaction volume for the day was 42,000 bales. The statistics of sales showed that Changfeng sold 5,350 bales, Tongfu 1,050 bales, Mingde 900 bales, Yuande 950 bales, Dachang 1,250 bales, Tongxing 1,450 bales, and Xincheng 1,450 bales. The Delivery Chips for This Month Are Still Lacking The Spot Cotton Situation Is Stronger Than Yarn 184

The cotton market is showing weakness again due to the fall of American cotton. Although the Poage-Hildebrandt relief bill has passed, the New York market price softened again at the close. As a result, people's sentiment is weak. However, the delivery chips for this month are not yet sufficient, which is inversely proportional to the yarn market. Therefore, the market is more expensive. Japanese merchants are also covering their short positions. However, spot cotton trading is not active. The American cotton outlook is bearish, and the sellers' attitude is very stable.

Raw Cotton Slightly Declines The morning market opening price of raw cotton was affected by the falling American cotton market. Main Reasons for the Buoyant Flour Market 187

—Speculators Driving up Prices… Small Factories Cashing Out Forward Contracts—

Yesterday, the flour market opened in the morning with a slightly soft but stable trend across all months. Quotations for imported wheat from Chicago and Canada were down slightly by about one to two jiao compared to the previous day. Therefore, after opening, the market sentiment remained calm, slightly recovering by about half a cent compared to the previous day. Later, because large mills still did not release stocks, some were even buying, and speculative long positions in the market continued to absorb supplies, stabilizing sentiment and gradually driving up prices. By the afternoon opening, market speculators were still pushing up prices, and mills were also withdrawing near-term offers, leading to a buoyant market sentiment. Small factories were also withdrawing near-term offers, but selling quite a few forward contracts. Northern merchants were both buying and selling, but selling exceeded buying. Under the current circumstances, the market is entirely driven by sentiment. In reality, sales to customers are not particularly strong. As a result, the current month was up by 1.75 cents compared to the previous day, April was up by 1.25 cents, May and June were up by 1 cent, July was up by 1.5 cents, and August was up by 1.75 cents.

Wheat Futures Strengthen Following the Flour Market 188

Yesterday, the wheat futures market showed a positive trend in all months during both the morning and afternoon sessions. Although quotations for imported wheat were down slightly by about one to two jiao, the buoyant flour market inevitably changed market sentiment. The current month, with deliveries approaching, opened higher by two to three cents. Although trading in distant months was not particularly active, it also saw some upward movement. This is because the current short positions are not easily liquidated, and any buying by long positions can easily cause volatility. The closing results showed that June and July were up by 1 cent compared to the previous day, and August was up by 5 cents. The spot wheat market remains active, with limited arrivals and mills still eager to buy. An opening price of 3.48 yuan was quoted for Bengbu wheat, and 3.68 yuan for Shandong wheat, totaling 1,500 bags, handled by Huafeng.

Soybean Prices Rise by Three to Five Cents 189

Yesterday, soybean prices rose due to increased bids for standard grades, and market sentiment was optimistic. However, despite the tense market atmosphere, buyers seemed hesitant, suggesting a possible pattern of short-term gains followed by long-term weakness. Yesterday, top-grade Zhongguan soybeans rose by three to five cents, while lower grades remained unchanged. Transactions included one cart of Feihe soybeans and one cart of Mengcheng soybeans, purchased by local brokers. Additionally, 200 bags of Guide soybeans were for export, while 400 bags of Dangshan soybeans and one cart of Haozhou soybeans were purchased by mills.

Consistent Rise in Soybean Oil and Raw Bean Oil Market 190

Yesterday, in the soybean oil market, except for Niuzhuang oil, which maintained its original price, factory oil, Dalian oil, and Qishan oil all increased by two to three jiao. It was reported that due to a telegram from Dalian reporting price increases, market sentiment slightly stabilized. Peanut oil supplies decreased, while sales in Zhejiang remained strong, leading to a rise of two to three jiao. Ground oil prices were quite firm. Transactions included 220 pieces of Bo'er raw oil at a price of 9.50 yuan, 2,000 pieces of warehouse-stored raw oil at a price of 9.20 yuan, and 100 pieces of light-skinned raw oil at a price of 8.90 yuan.

Free Talk

One Hope 204

— Yuan Che

I was once surprised to hear that the German soldier Remarque, after laying down his gun, picked up a pen and was able to write the world-shaking masterpiece "All Quiet on the Western Front." Later, after reading Glaeser's "Class of 1902," I suddenly realized that Remarque, when he went to the battlefield, probably, like the average German youth, had literary masterpieces in his knapsack. Moreover, I believe that German education, from elementary school to middle school, pays absolutely more attention to the aspects of rhetoric than China does with its perfunctory attitude, so it is very common to produce one or two Remarques.

In China, there are undoubtedly many, many young people who have experienced various kinds of lives, but who have never produced a great work. The most obvious reason is, of course, that they have not received a good education. And even if they have received a good education, when they go to serve as soldiers, work as laborers, or struggle through life, they certainly do not have any literary masterpieces in their pockets, because fundamentally there are no masterpieces to bring. Therefore, instead of blaming the writers who are working hard for "the lack of great creations now," it would be better to scold the predecessors who did not leave behind many great creations.

However, fortunately, Chinese creations are flourishing day by day with the help of foreign legacies. Speaking of this, we, the group of young people who do not quite understand foreign languages and are seeking foreign legacies to engage in practice, cannot but thank the translators of the past ten years. Therefore, at present, I do not so much hope for the emergence of great creations, but I very much hope that more foreign literary masterpieces will be translated.

We are infants lacking breast milk, and we often cry out in hunger and cold in the back alleys!

Zhenjiang Correspondence 205

— Shen Lun

Zhenjiang is now the capital of Jiangsu Province. A provincial capital should have the characteristics of a provincial capital. Are those wide roads, those cars that shoot like arrows released from a bowstring, the characteristics of a provincial capital? No. The characteristic of a provincial capital should be thousands of civil servants wearing badges!! Those big and small officials carrying briefcases on their way to government offices.

The major government offices are concentrated in the Zhongshan Road area in the city. Although Zhongshan Road is sixteen meters wide, there are not many cars passing by; apart from the occasional commercial vehicle, there are only a few "official cars" belonging to the major government offices. Therefore, many dull-witted small citizens keep grumbling that the road was built with so much manpower and material resources, but in reality, only a very small number of special classes benefit! Moreover, the government has always been short of money. The compensation of ten yuan per room for houses that were "forcefully demolished" for the road construction is still "on the books" to this day.

Although Zhenjiang is south of the Yangtze River, the people's habits, customs, language, and way of life are all Jiangbei-ized. It is not uncommon to see women with bound feet here, just as in the north. It is well known that the people of Jiangbei have the virtue of "enduring hardship and hard work." Zhenjiang is only separated from Xinghua, Yangzhou, Gaoyou, Rugao, and other counties by a river, so all the more arduous work, such as pulling rickshaws and porterage, is contracted by the Jiangbei gangs. Most of the locals go out to do business, and they can "endure hardship and hard work" just like the people of Jiangbei who sail out on a small boat to travel and find food. Along the Beijing-Shanghai Railway, in places like Shanghai and Suzhou, Zhenjiang people have considerable influence in the business world. When they leave their hometowns, they usually only have a bedding roll and a net basket. When they return, they may bring back thousands upon thousands of silver dollars. This is because the people of Zhenjiang have a special talent for saving money, and they have to weigh a large amount of money three times before spending it. Therefore, there are many poor people among the locals, but there are also quite a few middle-class families. The standard of living is higher in the city than outside the city, partly because of the distance in transportation, and partly because there is a group of "non-locals" living in the city. The demand for materials (such as houses and food) exceeds the supply, resulting in higher prices.

The locals call female domestic servants "Gao Ma" uniformly; while "Xiaodajie" is called "Lianzi." These two terms are quite puzzling, and even the locals do not know where they come from. After the bankruptcy of the countryside, there were suddenly many more "Gao Ma" and "Lianzi." To hire a "Lianzi" only requires a salary of eight jiao to one yuan per month. The salary of a "Gao Ma" is at most two yuan per month. Although the wages are meager, at least they can eat their fill; this is much better than waiting to starve to death in the declining countryside. In Zhenjiang, it is really difficult to find a modern woman. Even if you sometimes come across a "westernized" woman in a leather coat and high heels, her accent is definitely not local, but belongs to the family members of those big and small officials. Even if a local woman is a daughter of a wealthy family, she often wears foot wrappings and cotton qipaos in winter; leather coats and high heels are extremely rare.

This city is not thoroughly new, and it is too vaguely old, probably similar to many provincial capitals in inland China.

Thoughts on the He Xu Creative Issue 206

— Yu Wenzhou

Recently, another unfortunate thing has happened in the literary world, which is the matter of "He Jiahai and Xu Zhuanpeng's novels being unclear." On the one hand, there is an absolute denial from the start, and on the other hand, a list of goods with quantities is presented, and those who "speak out of righteousness" are even using the Spring and Autumn annals' technique of "concealing the faults of relatives." This kind of thing that is still unclear to this day may never be clear. In the future, I think it will either be a win-win situation or both sides will make sacrifices, allowing the presiding gentleman to gain a prestigious name. In general, it will not be a good gift to the literary world. The main reason why this matter is called unfortunate lies in this.

Because the matter is still unclear (although there is Mr. Shiheng's "last resort" "disclosure" and Mr. Xu Zhuanpeng's "helpless" "confession," but Mr. He Jiahai's "statement" and "defense" of "presenting evidence" have not yet been seen), outsiders naturally cannot make a judgment. Fortunately, the matter has not yet ended. Let's talk about it after it has been disclosed clearly in the future. However, "things have come to this point," and we cannot help but have a few thoughts:

First, a few years ago, we saw in the newspaper that a Mr. Shi had specialized in stealing manuscripts, and the victims were Mr. Yu Dafu and others. Later, we heard that a love novel expert who enjoyed great fame in the Yomiuri market was buying other people's manuscripts at low prices, signing his own name, and selling them at high prices. Recently, we have learned from many articles that some people specialize in hiring many low-priced secretaries to translate or write books for themselves in order to gain both fame and wealth. This has simply become a very popular and shameless trend (naturally, this trend can easily poison a new writer, and we must sweep it away). According to Mr. Xu Zhuanpeng's confession: "Because he (referring to He Jiahai) knew Xu Zhimo, his articles had a way out not long after he arrived in Shanghai. Sometimes he was in a hurry to pay fees, rent, and buy meal tickets, but he did not have any existing articles on hand to exchange for money, so he took my articles." From this, we can infer that such a thing is possible. For example, an article may not be published under Xu Zhuanpeng's name first, but after being taken back and published in another magazine, it becomes He Jiahai's name. Moreover, the editor who thinks he knows does not know, which is one of the reasons that constitute this possibility. In order to sweep away this shameless trend, I think it is necessary to clarify thoroughly, otherwise it will fall into the same trap as general theft cases. It is said that in Shanghai, detectives often condone those big thieves and principals who have already been greeted and entertained, and only catch a few small thieves as examples for the owners to see in order to win the reward of their superiors and the praise of society. However, I hope that discerning critics will not fall into the suspicion of acting as detectives!

Second, Mr. Xu Zhuanpeng said it very well: "Both Jiahai and I should admit the 'sins' and mistakes.' We have already done the wrong thing, and we only hope that similar things will not happen again in the future." Although, from an outsider's perspective, it is very easy for Mr. Xu Zhuanpeng to admit these "sins" and "mistakes" (because this can, on the contrary, make him gain both fame and wealth), we still cannot but respect this frank expression. However, we hope that Mr. Xu Zhuanpeng will give us a little more frank facts. Judging from Mr. Shiheng's article alone, it first makes people know that there are still some facts that "have not been permitted by Zhuanpeng and are now inconvenient to disclose" that are being concealed by Mr. Shiheng. Moreover, according to Mr. Shiheng's narrative, Mr. Zhuanpeng wanted to withdraw the article because of the encouragement of his friends, but he hesitated when the action was about to be carried out, as if he had some unspeakable difficulties. What's more, Mr. Xu Zhuanpeng himself has also said that "it is difficult for outsiders to understand Jiahai's difficulties and our difficulties." All of these make people unable to help but doubt the degree of frankness of Mr. Xu Zhuanpeng. Third, the unclear matters of Mr. He Jiahai and Mr. Xu Zhuanpeng should be clarified. Whether it is for the entire literary world or for their future, it should be clarified. However, this requires a fair mind from the general public and the magnanimity of good critics. Mr. Shiheng started by questioning and investigating, and then only told others, without pointing out or criticizing. Finally, he took responsibility for an undisclosed pseudonym and disclosed the facts he knew. After publicly announcing it in a newspaper with hundreds of thousands of daily sales, he still declared that he was forced to do so as a last resort and advised others not to publicize the matter, which is even more despised. This has already lost the magnanimity of a critic. At the same time, he and his friend Mr. Qingdaofu unanimously praised Mr. Xu Zhuanpeng's articles extremely, but only made some one-sided and premature judgments on the behavior that should be responsible for both parties. If we further link up everything that Mr. Shiheng has recently criticized about Mr. Xu Zhuanpeng, it is very difficult to make people see the fair heart of Mr. Shiheng. Not long ago, some small publications also attacked Mr. He Jiahai for having a certain tendency, and that tendency was precisely the target that Mr. Shiheng has always attacked. For the sake of the critic's fate, Mr. Shiheng should at least not make people think that his speaking out of righteousness has a meaning and effect that is more for friends than for the literary world. As for the "sins" and "mistakes" of Mr. He Jiahai, although we can only wait for Mr. He Jiahai himself to "admit" or "quibble" before speaking, it is okay to give a few words of advice first: Mr. He is still a very promising new writer. He should have the courage and determination to admit his "mistakes" and "sins," to openly publish all the facts frankly and honestly, to accept all criticisms and even scolding lessons from all sides, and to work hard in a very promising direction. Otherwise, he will not only be despised by others, but he will not even be able to save himself.

Tentative Translation of the Book of Songs 207

— Yu Shixia

Papaya

(I)

He sent me a papaya,

I returned him the first piece of beautiful jade, ju.

It's not about returning the gift for the sake of decency,

But wanting to keep a permanent memento!

(II)

He sent me a honey peach,

I returned him the second piece of beautiful jade, yao.

It's not about returning the gift for the sake of decency,

But wanting to keep a permanent memento!

(III)

He sent me a sweet plum,

I returned him the third piece of beautiful jade, jiu.

It's not about returning the gift for the sake of decency,

But wanting to keep a permanent memento!

Little Lizzie 208

— Pu Feng

Little Lizzie, the old system prevents me from breaking free from you,

I can't bear to let you grieve and shed tears alone;

Let's just acknowledge the so-called marital relationship.

……………………

Frankly speaking, I pity you,

I know, I, I won't love you,

After all, I can only continue to perfunctorily deal with you.

……………………

True, endless field work has buried you,

True, the earthworms in the fields are familiar with your sorrowful tears,

But who do you blame? ——Blame your own fate!

……………………

You won't believe it, the world may change.

One day, you will automatically separate from me,

You have a healthy body, maybe I can't catch up with you!

……………………

——Ah! Don't grieve, Little Lizzie!

Western Journey Jottings (II) 209

— Lu Yan

Ge Buxi kept throwing the books I didn't need into my suitcase. He put them in, I took them out, and after a while, he put them in my suitcase again. He seemed to think that these were the books I usually read and should take with me. But how could he know that I don't need them now; and how could I myself know that I will need them in the future?

Lan and my mother repeatedly told me to take care of my health, eat well, and sleep early. However, who can know that people who love health are prone to illness, while people who don't love health live long?

Everything is unknowable. But we all hope for a good future.

Therefore, I also hope that my journey will be safe and that I will encounter happy things.

II. In the Shanghai-Beiping Train

As soon as I entered the carriage, it was as if I had arrived in Beiping. Almost all the waiters on the train spoke fluent and harmonious Beiping dialect. It had been seven or eight years since I had heard such pure words. It made me feel happy and trustful. Although I was still in Shanghai, it was like arriving in the refreshing and honest northern country.

The train was about to leave, and I suddenly remembered that I had written the wrong date on the telegram just now. I couldn't come back if I got off myself, so I asked the waiter if there was a solution. "You write a note, and I'll ask him to take it. He's one of us, the cleaner, and he definitely won't make a mistake!"

I absolutely believed that he wouldn't make a mistake, even though he wouldn't see me again. If it were a southerner, I would have to be suspicious.

The train moved slowly, faster. The lights representing Shanghai that night gradually faded and became desolate. Soon we were speeding through the darkness.

Lao Ye kept reciting his poems to me frankly. He was truly a big child. He made me feel old. Ten years ago, I was about the same as him, saying whatever I wanted, but now I am always silent. I don't want others to know my history and life, thoughts and feelings. I have learned the techniques of life.

He said that his child couldn't hear the birds singing, and he was worried about the child. This is really a sad thing. My child is like this too. Many children are like this too. Parents often think that schools in the city are better than schools in the countryside. They love the city themselves, so they bring their children to the city. But they don't know that schools in the city have nothing but a few magnificent school buildings. Even if they are lucky enough to be really good, it is still sad without a natural environment to nurture the children. (To be continued)

Last Testament 210

— Lin Weiyin

To prevent herself from having any more excuses so she could settle down and write the article she had planned, Yina stayed up almost until dawn yesterday before returning home. However, now, even though she had forced her mother and younger siblings back to their own rooms, and had arranged cigarettes, tea, paper, and pen on the table, she still could not calm her heart, and even could not bring herself to sit in the chair in front of the table.

"If I don't write now, what will become of me!" she warned herself.

But she was still pacing back and forth, refusing to let her body sit down, as if the chair cushion was a beehive, and she would be stung if she sat down.

"Why is it that on a Sunday evening, not a single person calls?" The longing that had been in her subconscious was no longer subconscious. —Yes, she was hoping that someone, anyone, would call her and ask her out, so she could find a rescue.

"How stupid to choose a Sunday to start working!" she began to blame herself. "If others don't call me, why don't I call them myself? Okay, I'll just stay up another night, and definitely start writing tomorrow."

So she decided to make a call, and as she walked towards the telephone, she had already decided on the person she wanted to call.

"Is this the Song residence?—Please let Miss Three answer the phone.—Is that Huiqun?—This is Yina.—I'm at home. Yes, I'm all alone.—I was just about to ask you out.—Tell me.—Dahua?—Oh, Dahu, okay.—First come, first served.—At the entrance inside."

Yina was the first to arrive at Dahu. After waiting for a while, she saw Xiao Songchen and Hou Ziji arriving.

"Oh, Miss Chen. Are you alone? Waiting for Ye Chu?" Ziji said first.

Yina shook her head.

"Then, has Ye Chu already arrived?" Songchen added.

"No; I don't know," Yina said. "I'm waiting for Huiqun."

"How about we go inside together and wait?" Songchen suggested to her.

"We agreed to wait here; or you can go in first if you like."

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talk

Prohibition of Banquets, Opium, Gambling, and the Dawn Movement 211

— Chen

The galloping iron hooves of the Northeast Four Provinces and the bombing of Shanghai once awakened the Chinese government and public from their drunken dream of pleasure, shouting slogans of enduring humiliation and bearing heavy burdens, sleeping on brushwood and tasting gall, and working diligently day and night to raise funds for the cause. For a time, it was carried out with great fanfare, like something important was happening. Unfortunately, this call failed to awaken the deaf and enlighten the blind, and could not reverse the decline. Following the departure of the Japanese cannon fire, it disappeared without a trace, even vanishing altogether. One only needs to open their eyes to see that movie theaters, dance halls, art venues, and large stages are more prosperous than ever before. Grand hotels and restaurants, singing platforms and dancing pavilions, are still filled with songs and dances, and orchestras everywhere. Where is there any sign of national crisis or foreign invasion? It is simply a scene of peace and prosperity from the Tang and Yu dynasties!

However, one is born in sorrow and dies in ease. Moreover, at this time of "imminent peril" and "multiple disasters," some officials who are "vigilant and diligent, finding it difficult to sleep or eat" have embraced the "grand aspiration" of changing customs and habits, "cleansing away old filth," "revitalizing the spirit," and "rectifying themselves to lead by example." Recently, it has been reported that in Kaifeng, Henan, various government agencies are vigorously implementing the "Dawn Movement." Military and political leaders conduct morning exercises for one hour every day, followed by specialized academic lectures. When the chairman inspects Mengjin, he also admonishes the county magistrate and civil servants. Han Qingtian of Shandong Province has repeatedly emphasized and advocated "vitality," and the Military Affairs Committee also reiterated the previous order on the second day of this month: (order omitted). Judging from this order, it has gathered the great achievements of Chinese society's bad habits, purely living an extremely decadent and depraved life. Some are inextricably linked with "opium" girls from India, spending their days intoxicated in a haze of smoke and mist, with a dim lamp, a single couch, and a situation where they are active at night and inactive during the day, resembling a skeleton three parts human and seven parts ghost. Some are addicted to gambling, either playing mahjong in rounds, or shouting and drinking while playing dice, making games of chance. The dog racing tracks, pelota courts, and large gambling dens in this big city are even more their destinations. And those who generally hunt for beauty and pursue those with "the disease of the lonely one" have long become "regulars" at the brothels. Many popular courtesans also regard bureaucratic politicians as "extremely welcome" guests. As for the small banquets every three days and the large banquets every five days, used by those who see them as a way to "connect feelings" in order to seek advancement, they are even more numerous. This morbid phenomenon, if left unchecked, has actually become an "accepted fact." It is a necessary condition for those "aspiring to politics." Lacking these skills creates a situation where one can "forget about mixing in officialdom."

These bad habits directly manifest as procrastination and wasted time, but under their influence, they lead to political corruption, the exploitation of the common people, and the decline and death of the nation and people.

However, the emergence of this particular phenomenon has its own economic background. It not only occurs in a certain circle, but is also prevalent in a certain class. Therefore, its fundamental eradication will not be achieved by the "rectification" of a few leaders who "cleanse away old filth," but only by changing the economic system that is mutually causal.

Impressions of the Performance of "Ladies and Gentlemen" 212

— Gaoyuan

First of all, we cannot help but admire the enthusiasm of the Youth Association's Intellectual Education Department in promoting drama. After the many difficulties of script selection and rehearsal mentioned in the "opening speech," they were finally able to stage such a new script as "Ladies and Gentlemen," giving us a visual feast. Moreover, "on the one hand, we hope that the audience can arouse interest in studying drama, and actively participate, so as to form a drama research association." We hope that this performance can further achieve this goal, and that another strong new force will be added to the drama movement. How happy we should be!

According to the author, the script of "Ladies and Gentlemen" was written in a hurry, like the "original manuscript written on wax paper." However, the result is that the script does not have many shortcomings due to being written in a "hurry." From the impression gained on the stage, this script is quite successful.

The story unfolded in the three-act play must be considered quite complex. The life of a factory owner's family, factory affairs, and the entire noble social stratum, the shaking situation of the industrial and financial circles under the current domestic and foreign economic and political internal contradictions, and the struggles of workers in the factory, etc., are all handled quite thoroughly by the author, without appearing to be piled up or wordy. Various situations are expressed with very short dialogues and actions. This economical handling of the subject matter is the primary reason for the success of this script.

The character portrayals in the play are also clear enough, only the factory owner Zhou Zhenhua is not sufficiently portrayed. Or rather, it is quite inappropriate and worth discussing. A 51-year-old Chinese industrial tycoon, even if he is old, and the bankruptcy of the factory is due to the political and economic panic, which cannot be saved by individual efforts, I don't think he should be someone who doesn't even know "how he got rich" or "when his son was born." In this way, it will make the audience think that his industrial bankruptcy is due to his own incompetence and poor management, which is very possible. I wonder what the author thinks about this.

In addition, Zhou's wife, who smokes opium and chants Buddhist scriptures, the concubine who eloped with the secretary, and his daughter Zhou Liying, the most popular socialite in high society, are all very clearly portrayed. The secretary who seduced the concubine to elope and the creditors who pressed for debt seem to be slightly less characterized. As for Wang Ma and the chauffeur, the opening scene introduces the lives of the servants with their ambiguous behavior of hiding behind the screen to kiss and hug, which is very interesting and characteristic. The opening and closing of each scene are very natural and compact. The opening of the second act introduces the nanny's family situation and provokes the concubine's scolding; instead of the borrower, the creditor comes; agreeing to mortgage the property and encountering a workers' strike; the concubine elopes, and the first wife comes out with a smoking pipe in hand to curse; and the loan has not been received, and the borrower commits suicide because of the failure of the bid speculation; these are all tense and able to capture the audience's emotions.

The whole play quite exposes the incurable corrupt life of the noble people, the bankruptcy of China's national industry, the economic panic in the financial capitalist society, the "money-meat" relationship between men and women in high society, and the rise of another new social force.

Precisely because of the above meaning, if the occurrence of the workers' strike was at the very end of the play, I think it would be more tense and more important. Although the workers' strike occurred, Mr. Zhou still thought that as long as the loan was obtained and the workers' demands were met, the factory would still not have problems, until the borrower's bid speculation failed and he committed suicide, he had no final solution. Here, there is a shadow of the author taking the lighter and avoiding the heavier.

The scenery and lighting seem to have taken some effort, but the scenery of the first act (same as the third act) seems to represent an old-fashioned family, and cannot fully represent the residence of a big capitalist. Of course, China's national capitalists have a feudal atmosphere, and Mrs. Zhou still chants Buddhist scriptures, but the whole scene is full of the atmosphere of a feudal family, focusing on the old aspect.

In addition, the plaster statue in the second act is for decoration and is too dim. When Wang Ma took out the telephone in the third act, it was very clear that it was made of light paper, and the bottom was wood-yellow; the child held in her arms was also light, and the actors did not handle it carefully; the sound effects of the child's crying and the car horn were not like the real thing, but these are all minor details.

The playwright and director have put in great effort. The performances of the actors Liu Yin, Zhou Dao, and Hong Dou were all very successful, but Liu Yin's makeup was not old enough, and Zhou Boxun's makeup seemed to be more greasy and bloody. If the costumes were more gorgeous, it would better enrich his capitalist character. The appearance of being poor and frustrated in the first act reduced the effect considerably. Jinshan's secretary has not fully shown his ability to seduce the concubine to elope and how to curry favor with the factory owner in front of the factory owner. Sha Bai's creditor also has not

Page 18

done his best to press for debt. I think this is related to the actors' characters. The rest, Li Ping's nanny's voice was a little low, and the Mandarin was not clear in a few places, but because of her sorrowful character, these did not cause much harm. The abandoned Wang Ma and Zhuo Jianchao's chauffeur were both good. I regret that I only watched the first show on the first day. I think the later shows must have improved a lot. Overall, the performance of this play was quite successful, and many places where effects should have been achieved did not slip away. Here we can see the dim future of China's national industry, the irredeemable economic panic, and the corrupt life of the upper class. The playwright, director, and actors are all very hardworking. (End)

Death 213

— Yi

Death, a common death, the death of a small animal being brutally killed.

This death, even if it befalls someone, may not be more than "common" or "great." But now, it is only the death of a cat.

This cat, a stray cat on the street, lives in a black-spotted fur coat with its thin limbs. Its four small legs are connected to a flat stomach, which is obviously an animal that is often unable to eat its fill. I saw it smelling and pawing around the trash can; I also saw it hiding under the eaves at night with its eyes closed. But whenever I passed by or approached it, it would always run far away from me and then stop and turn around to look at me. It would meow, I heard it, like other cats, but the sound was weaker. Especially, when someone gave it something to eat, it would meow in a grateful tone. —It would do these things, only these things. It was too weak! It could not drag live chickens to eat, and could not steal goldfish to eat, so it deserved to be so thin!

But, good, the fate of this little animal had a turning point—it seemed to have a period where it could live a comfortable life. That was because an old woman who lived in the same house as me took it in because she pitied it for being hungry. So, now, it had changed from a stray life to a leisurely life: when it wanted to eat, there was ready-made white rice waiting for it to fill its stomach; when it wanted to sleep, there was a comfortable nest specially made for it. How lucky! This little animal's body had a home.

"Humans are indeed great and kind!" It should think like this now: "God! I thank you, thank you for giving birth to humans in this universe!" Indeed, it was going to be extremely happy, much more lively than before. Sometimes I would also stroke it with my hand, and it no longer feared and avoided me like before, and even raised its head and meowed a few times. Looking at its appearance, it seemed very satisfied with its current life. Time was flying forward day by day, and the fur on this little animal's body gradually became shiny, and its body slowly became fat. Undoubtedly, the current life had shown its influence on its physiology. Here, I absolutely did not think that after this leisurely life, there would be a crisis lurking that would ruin this little animal!

The old woman who gave it food every day probably left home for some reason and did not return for more than a month. Not only was no one taking care of this little animal's food and lodging, but it was also immediately driven out. The reason was that it would poop and pee everywhere.

From then on, its footprints often appeared next to the trash can and under the eaves. It still smelled, pawed, stretched, and closed its eyes, just like before, without resentment. Not only did it not resent, but it was also able to not forget that it had once lived in the house. So it still came often, continuously. Finally, people developed an extremely disgusted feeling towards it: the next time they saw it coming, they would break its legs.

Small animals are always small animals. It has no reason and even less knows about the fickleness of human feelings. One morning it ran over and finally gave its own life.

There was always a reason for everything. On that morning, people discovered that one piece was missing from a chicken stewed in a pot. After speculation, it was determined that the cat had eaten it. So the crime was sentenced, just waiting for execution.

Catching a cat was of course extremely easy. It was captured when it ran over. Then two ropes were tied to its four legs, and one person grabbed its tail and dragged it out of the door.

"Are you really going to execute it?" I finally asked.

This person did not answer me, but took this tied-up little animal and walked out. After a while, the sound of a stick beating reached my ears.

"Dead," this person said when he returned.

"…………"

Ah! Common death, just a small animal

The death of being brutally killed.
